+++
title = "+०२ आत्मसिद्धिः"
+++


**परमाचार्य श्रीमद्यामुनाचार्य समनुगृहीते,**

**सिद्धित्रये आत्मसिद्धिः**



## जीव-प्रमाणम्
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

THE PRAMANA BY WHICH THE EXISTENCE OF THE JIVA IS ESTABLISHED
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

किं पुनर् अस्मिन् देहादि-व्यतिरेकिणि चेतने प्रत्यगात्मनि प्रमाणम्? ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P66]] What is the means of knowledge (pramāņa) by which this individual self, which is distinct from the body and the like, and which is intelligent, is established?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

किं पुनरस्मिन्देहादिव्यतिरेकिणि चेतने प्रत्यगात्मनि प्रमाणम्? ।
</details>

### नैयायिकानुमानम्

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

(a) The Nyaya view that the soul is established through inference-
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[अनु मानमिति|अनुमानम् इति]] नय-विचक्षणो ऽक्षपादः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Akṣapāda, who is master of the science of logic, thinks that it is inference.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनु मानमिति नयविचक्षणोऽक्षपादः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यद्-आह " इच्छा-द्वेष-प्रयत्न-सुख-दुःख-[[ज्ञाना न्यात्मनो|ज्ञानान्य् आत्मनो]] लिङ्ग [[लिङ्ग "म् इति|म्" इति]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

What he says is-"Desire, hate, pleasure, pain and knowledge are the reasons pointing to the existence of the soul."[^66_118]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^66_118]: Icchadvesaprayatnasukhajñānānyātmano liñāni *Nyāya*-*Sutra*, I. i. *10*
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यदाह " इच्छाद्वेषप्रयत्नसुखदुःखज्ञाना न्यात्मनो लिङ्ग "म् इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

किम् अमीषाम् आत्मनाविनाभावो धूमध्वज-विशेषेणेव धूम-विशेषस्य दृष्टः?
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Has invariable concomitance between these and the soul, like that between smoke and fire (dhūmadhvaja), been observed anywhere?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

किममीषामात्मनाविनाभावो धूमध्वजविशेषेणेव धूमविशेषस्य दृष्टः?
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

हन्तैवं तत एव तत्-प्रमितेः किम् अनुमानेन? ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Indeed, if so, as the knowledge of the self is obtained thence itself, what is the need for inference?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

हन्तैवं तत एव तत्प्रमितेः किमनुमानेन? ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

मा भूद् विशेषतो दर्शनम्; सामान्यतस् तु भविष्यति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(The opponent replies) no invariable concomitance may have been observed in particular (between qualities such as desire, etc., and the soul); but, in general (i.e., between qualities and their substrate), it may be noticed.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

माभूद्विशेषतोदर्शनम्; सामान्यतस्तु भविष्यति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[तथाहिइच्छादयः|तथा हि — इच्छादयः]] कार्यत्वानित्यत्व-गुणत्वादिभिः शब्दादय इवाऽश्रिततयानुमीयन्ते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

To make the point clear... Desire and other qualities, like sound and so on, are inferred to be dependent upon something, for the reason of their being effects, non-eternal (entities) attributes, and so on.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाहिइच्छादयः कार्यत्वानित्यत्वगुणत्वादिभिः शब्दादय इवाऽश्रिततयानुमीयन्ते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यश् चैषाम् आश्रयः स आत्मा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That which is the substrate of these (qualities) is the self.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यश्चैषामाश्रयः स आत्मा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

गुणत्वं च परिशेषात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That desire and the like are qualities is inferred by elimination.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

गुणत्वं च परिशेषात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न सामान्य-विशेष-समवायाभावाः अनित्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Being non-eternal, they cannot be either generality *(sāmānya*), or particularity (*višeṣa*), or inherence (samavāya), or non-existence (abhāva).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न सामान्यविशेषसमवायाभावाः अनित्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न द्रव्यं कर्म वा, व्यापक-द्रव्य-समवायाद् इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

As they are inherent in all-pervasive substances, they cannot be either substance *(dravya*) or action (karma).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न द्रव्यं कर्म वा, व्यापकद्रव्यसमवायादिति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

विशेष-गुणत्वं च अनित्यत्वे सत्य् अस्मद्-आद्य् एकेन्द्रिय-[[ग्राह्यत्वनियमात्रूपादिवत्|ग्राह्यत्व-नियमाद् रूपादि-वत्]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That they are specific qualities *(višeṣaguņa*) is established by the fact that at all times, like colour and other qualities, they, while being non-eternal, are grasped by one of our senses.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

विशेषगुणत्वं च अनित्यत्वे सत्यस्मदाद्येकेन्द्रियग्राह्यत्वनियमात्रूपादिवत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

After proving in general terms that consciousness, being a guņa, must have a substrate, it is shown by a process of elimination that it must be a specific entity, namely ātmā :—
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एवम् आश्रय-मात्रम् उपस्थापयन्तो ऽन्वय-व्यतिरेकिणो हेतवः द्रव्यान्तर-गुणत्वं च प्रत्याचक्षाणैः केवल-व्यतिरेकि-साधनैर् आत्म-गोचरतया नियम्यन्ते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The reasons concomitant in affirmation and negation *(anvayavyatirekino hetavaḥ*), which, in this manner, indicate only (the need of) some substrate (for desire, etc.), are narrowed down in their scope in such a way as to refer to the soul by the reasons which are concomitant in negation only (*kevalavyatirekisādhanaiḥ*) and which disprove the view that they are qualities of substances other than the soul.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

एवमाश्रयमात्रमुपस्थापयन्तोऽन्वयव्यतिरेकिणो हेतवः द्रव्यान्तरगुणत्वं च प्रत्याचक्षाणैः केवलव्यतिरेकिसाधनैरात्मगोचरतया नियम्यन्ते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा हि [[भवतिइच्छादयो|भवति — इच्छादयो]] न महा-भूत-गुणाः, स्वात्मन एव प्रत्यक्षत्वात्; [[अबाह्येन्द्रियग्राह्यत्वाद्धा|अबाह्येन्द्रिय-ग्राह्यत्वाद् वा]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That this is so is evident from the following :- Desire and the like are not the qualities of the primal elements (mahābhūtas), because they are perceived only by oneself, or because they are not to be grasped by the outer senses.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथा हि भवतिइच्छादयो न महाभूतगुणाः, स्वात्मन एव प्रत्यक्षत्वात्; अबाह्येन्द्रियग्राह्यत्वाद्धा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ये भूत-गुणास् ते स्वात्म-परात्म-प्रत्यक्षाः बाह्य-करण-प्रत्यक्षाश् च, यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P67]] The qualities belonging to the primal elements, such as colour and the like, are perceivable by oneself and others and are perceived by the outer senses'; but desire and the like are not so (perceivable); hence, they are not the qualities of primal elements.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ये भूतगुणास्ते स्वात्मपरात्मप्रत्यक्षाः बाह्यकरणप्रत्यक्षाश्च, यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न तथेच्छादय इति न तद्-गुणाः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

but desire and the like are not so (perceivable); hence, they are not the qualities of primal elements.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न तथेच्छादय इति न तद्गुणाः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

दिक्-काल-मनांसि पुनः न विशेष-गुणवन्ति; नापि तद्-गुणानां प्रत्यक्षत्वम् इति न तेषामपि गुणाः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Again, space (dik), time and mind (manas) do not have specific qualities; and their attributes are not open to perception; hence, desire and the like are not their qualities.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

दिक्कालमनांसि पुनः न विशेषगुणवन्ति; नापि तद्गुणानां प्रत्यक्षत्वमिति न तेषामपि गुणाः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[अकारणगुणपूर्वत्वातयावच्छरीरभावित्वादित्यादयः|अकारणगुणपूर्वत्वाद् अयावच्छरीरभावित्वादित्यादयः]] शरीर-विशेष-गुणत्व-प्रतिषेध-हेतवः प्राचीनाश् चात्रानुक्रष्टव्याः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Reasons, such as the following---since they are not dependent on the causal substances; since they do not exist as long as the body lasts--(reasons) which were cited before, and which refute the view that they are specific qualities of the body, are to be brought forward and applied here also.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अकारणगुणपूर्वत्वातयावच्छरीरभावित्वादित्यादयः शरीरविशेषगुणत्वप्रतिषेधहेतवः प्राचीनाश्चात्रानुक्रष्टव्याः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तेनेच्छादयो न शरीर-गुणाः तद्-गुण-भावापवाद-प्रमाण-वत्त्वे सति गुणत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Therefore, desire and the like are not the qualities of the body; for, while there is evidence contradicting the view that they are the qualities of the body, they are qualities.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तेनेच्छादयो न शरीरगुणाः तद्गुणभावापवादप्रमाणवत्त्वे सति गुणत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ये यथोक्त-साध्या न भवन्ति, ते यथोक्त-साधना अपि न भवन्ति; यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Whatever does not possess the sadhya does not have the aforesaid sadhana either, as in the case of colour.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ये यथोक्तसाध्या न भवन्ति, ते यथोक्तसाधना अपि न भवन्ति; यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यथोक्त-साधनाः पुनर् इच्छादय इति यथोक्त-साध्या एवेति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Desires and the like, however, possess the aforesaid hetu, and hence, they possess the sādhya.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यथोक्तसाधनाः पुनरिच्छादय इति यथोक्तसाध्या एवेति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

विमति-पदास्पदेभ्यः [[शरीरादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणत्वप्रतिज्ञापि|शरीरादिभ्यो ऽर्थान्तर-गुणा]] इच्छादय इति वा प्रतिज्ञा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Or, the thesis to be proved (instead of being 'Desire and the like are not the qualities of the body') may be the following--Desire and the like are qualities of some substance other than the body, which is the point under dispute.[^67_119]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^67_119]: The point in dispute is not the existence of the body, but its possessing desires etc., as attributes.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

विमतिपदास्पदेभ्यः शरीरादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणा इच्छादय इति वा प्रतिज्ञा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यथोक्त एव हेतुः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The aforesaid hetu and illustrative example may be cited (in the case of this thesis also).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यथोक्त एव हेतुः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

उदाहरणं च प्रयोक्तव्यम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The aforesaid hetu and illustrative example may be cited (in the case of this thesis also).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

उदाहरणं च प्रयोक्तव्यम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

सामान्येन वा अन्वयः [[प्रदर्शनीयःयो|प्रदर्शनीयः — यो]] यद्-गुण-भावापवादक-प्रमाण-वत्त्वे सति गुणः, [[ततोर्ऽथान्तरस्य|स ततो ऽर्थान्तरस्य]] गुणः; यथा पृथिव्य् आदिभ्यः शब्द इति आकाश-सिद्धि-वद् आत्म-सिद्धिर् इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Positive concomitance too may be shown in a somewhat general way. That which is a quality, when there is evidence contradicting the view that it is the quality of a given entity, is the attribute of something other than that given entity, just as sound is the quality of something other than earth and the like. In this way, just as ether (ākāśa) is proved (to be the substrate of sound), the self is established (to be the substrate of desire and the like.)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

सामान्येन वान्वयः प्रदर्शनीयःयो यद्गुणभावापवादकप्रमाणवत्त्वे सति गुणः, स ततोर्ऽथान्तरस्य गुणः; यथा पृथिव्यादिभ्यः शब्द इति आकाशसिद्धिवदात्मसिद्धिरिति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मन आनुमानिकत्व-पक्ष-निरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मन आनुमानिकत्वपक्षनिरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मन आनुमानिकत्वपक्षनिरूपणम्)
</details>

#### खण्डनम्

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Refutation of the Nyaya view
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

इदमपि न समीचीनम् इत्य् एके ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Some consider that this (view) is not correct.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

इदमपि न समीचीनमित्येके ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[तथाहिअन्वयव्यतिरेकिहेतुभिर्देहादिसाधारणमाश्रयमात्रमवगमितम्|तथा हि — अन्वय-व्यतिरेकि-हेतुभिर् देहादि-साधारणम् आश्रय-मात्रम् अवगमितम्]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

To elucidate this point,--with the aid of reasons concomitant in affirmation and negation *(anvayavyatireki*) it was only made known that there must be some support (for desire and other qualities), which might be either the body or some other substance.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाहिअन्वयव्यतिरेकिहेतुभिर्देहादिसाधारणमाश्रयमात्रमवगमितम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च तावता ऽत्म-सिद्धिः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

By this reasoning alone the soul is not established (to be that substrate).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न च तावताऽत्मसिद्धिः ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Argument from pure negative concomitance fares no better :—
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

केवल-व्यतिरेकी तु साधन-दशाम् एव नासादयति, सपक्षान्वय-विरहात्, असाधारण-वत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P68]] The reason concomitant in negation alone *(kevalavyatireki*) does not even possess the quality of being a correct reason; for, as in the fallacy called *asādhārana,* there is absence of the probans in instances where the sadhya is surely met with (sapaksa).[^68_120]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^68_120]: In the argument, sound is eternal, because it is sound the hetu is vitiated by the fallacy of asādhāreņa; for, it is not present in any sapaksa (i.c., similar examples where the sadhya is present) even as it is not present in the vipaksa. Similarly, in cases where reasons concomitant in negation alone (*kevalavyatireki*) are employed, there being no sapaksa, it is impossible to show the presence of the hetu in apaksas. Hence, *kevalavyatireki* is considered fallacious. It is defective for another reason also. In order to show that wherever the sadhya is absent the hetu is also absent the sadhya must first have been understood previously; but it is not met with anywhere. Hence, the Vedantins dismiss kevalavyatirkī as being faulty. Cf. 'sadhyābhāvo vipakse kathamiva viditaḥ tasya sadhyaprasiddheh' *Tattvamuktākaļāpa, Buddhisara*, verse 53. See also *Nyaya*-*Parisuddhi* (Memorial edition, pp. 66-75) and *Didhiti*. The *Vedanta* Paribhāṣā rejects *kevalānvayi* also, on the score that the kevalanvayi requires a sadhya which is present everywhere and such a sadhya is inadmissible on the theory that Brahman is nirguna.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

केवलव्यतिरेकी तु साधनदशामेव नासादयति, सपक्षान्वयविरहात्, असाधारणवत् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[नचैवं|न च एवम्]] केवलान्वयिनो विपक्ष-व्यतिरेक-दर्शन-विकलतया साधारण-वद् असाधनत्वम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The objection that on this admission, even the reason concomitant in affirmation alone cannot be considered as correct: for, as in the fallacy known as *sadharana*, there is the failure to show the absence of the reason in the counter-example (vipaksa)[^68_121]---(this objection) does not stand.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^68_121]: The opponent says 'In the argument the mountain has fire, because it is knowable', the hetu is defective *(sādhārṇa*), because it is not absent in the vipakṣa. Similarly, in arguments employing reasons concomitant in affirmation alone *(*kevalanvayi), there being no vipaksa, the absence of the hetu in the vipaksa cannot be cited. Hence, kevalānvayi also is a defective process of reasoning.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नचैवं केवलान्वयिनो विपक्षव्यतिरेकदर्शनविकलतया साधारणवदसाधनत्वम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[देशकालादिशङ्गितोपाधिविगमेप्यन्वयदर्शनेन|देश-कालादि-शङ्कितोपाधि-विगमे ऽप्य् अन्वय-दर्शनेन]] साध्यान्वित-स्वभावतया परिनिश्चितत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Since, even in the absence of suspected limiting conditions (upadhís), such as space, time and the like, the co-presence (of the hetu and the sadhya) is found, it is definitely ascertained that the hetu has the character of being connected with the sadhya.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

देशकालादिशङ्गितोपाधिविगमेप्यन्वयदर्शनेन साध्यान्वितस्वभावतया परिनिश्चितत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च साधनाभावे साध्याभाव-दर्शन-मात्रेण साध्यान्वित-स्वभावत्वं शक्यं निश्चेतुम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

From the mere observation of the absence of the sadhya when there is the absence of the hetu, it is not possible to ascertain that the hetu has the character of being connected with the sadhya.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच साधनाभावे साध्याभावदर्शनमात्रेण साध्यान्वितस्वभावत्वं शक्यं निश्चेतुम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अभावस्यानन्तदेशव्यापितयानवयवेन ग्रहणस्यैव दुष्करत्वात्, कलयाप्य् अन्यत्र-वृत्तौ सम्बन्धे नियमासम्भवात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P69]] As the non-existence of the sadhya is met with in innumerable places, it is impossible even to take note of them all exhaustively. If even in a single place the hetu were to be present in some manner, the universality of the connection cannot be maintained.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अभावस्यानन्तदेशव्यापितयानवयवेन ग्रहणस्यैव दुष्करत्वात्, कलयाप्यन्यत्रवृत्तौ सम्बन्धे नियमासम्भवात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[सन्देहग्रस्तत्वाच्चकिं|सन्देह-ग्रस्तत्वाच् च किम्]] साधनाभाव-प्रयुक्तः साध्याभावः, किं वा निमित्तान्तर-प्रयुक्त इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, it is a matter for doubt whether the non-existence of the sadhya is due to the absence of the hetu or to some other cause.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

सन्देहग्रस्तत्वाच्चकिं साधनाभावप्रयुक्तः साध्याभावः, किं वा निमित्तान्तरप्रयुक्त इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[पृथिव्यादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणत्वप्रतिज्ञापि|पृथिव्यादिभ्यो ऽर्थान्तर-गुणत्व-प्रतिज्ञापि]] द्रव्यान्तराप्रसिद्धेर् अप्रसिद्ध-विशेषणा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even the thesis (that desire and the like) are the qualities of some entity other than earth and the like may be charged with having an unproven attribute (aprasiddha-*viseṣaṇa*), for that other entity has not been proved.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

पृथिव्यादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणत्वप्रतिज्ञापि द्रव्यान्तराप्रसिद्धेरप्रसिद्धविशेषणा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति नैयायिकाभिमतात्मानुमान-निरासः)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति नैयायिकाभिमतात्मानुमाननिरासः)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति नैयायिकाभिमतात्मानुमाननिरासः)
</details>

### साङ्ख्यम् अनुमानम्

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

(b) The Sankhya View

The Sankhya mode of proof stands discredited for the same reasons :-
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एतेन साङ्ख्योदीरित-साधन-भेदा अप्य् अपोदिता वेदितव्याः सङ्घात-परार्थत्वादयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

By the same reasoning, even the various reasons (such as collocations exist for the sake of others) are to be understood as having been set aside.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

एतेन साङ्ख्योदीरितसाधनभेदा अप्यपोदिता वेदितव्याः सङ्घातपरार्थत्वादयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा च तान् एव तावद् आदितो व्याकुर्महे
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Let us analyse them in the order of their presentation.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथा च तानेव तावदादितो व्याकुर्महे
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The Sankhya proofs for the existence of soul.
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[सङ्गातपरार्थत्वात्र्रिगुणादिविपर्ययादधिष्ठानात्|सङ्घात-परार्थत्वात् त्रिगुणादि-विपर्ययाद् अधिष्ठानात्]] । पुरुषो ऽस्ति भोक्तृ-भावात् कैवल्यार्थं प्रवृत्तेश् च ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>


"Since collocations exist for the sake of something other than themselves, since (in this other) there is the absence of the three gunas and the like, since there must be control (of these collocations), since there must be an experiencer, and since there is activity for securing aloofness (from --prakṛti), the soul exists."[^69_122]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^69_122]: *Sankhya*-*Kārikā*, verse 17.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

" सङ्गातपरार्थत्वात्र्रिगुणादिविपर्ययादधिष्ठानात् ।  
पुरुषोऽस्ति भोक्तृभावात्कैवल्यार्थं प्रवृत्तेश्च ॥ "
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[अयम्अर्थःदेहेन्द्रियादयः|अयम् अर्थः — देहेन्द्रियादयः]] परार्थाः [[सङ्गातत्वाच्छयनासनशरणादिवत्|सङ्घातत्वाच् छयनासन-शरणादि-वत्]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

This means--Being collocations, the body, the senses and so on, like a bed, a seat, a house, etc., exist for the sake of something other than themselves.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अयम्अर्थःदेहेन्द्रियादयः परार्थाः सङ्गातत्वाच्छयनासनशरणादिवत् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

प्रत्यक्षं च शरीरस्य सङ्घातत्वं, भूतानां च ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The character of being a collocation attributed to the body and the primal elements is vouched for by perception.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

प्रत्यक्षं च शरीरस्य सङ्घातत्वं, भूतानां च ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अव्यक्त-महद्-अहङ्कारेन्द्रियाणां च सुख-दुःख-मोहात्मतया तथात्वम् अनुमेयं तद्वद् एव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That the same character (of being a collocation) belongs to unmanifest prakṛti (avyakta), mahat, ahamkāra and the senses, as to the body and elements, is to be inferred from the fact that the former are of the nature of pleasure, misery and delusion.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अव्यक्तमहदहङ्कारेन्द्रियाणां च सुखदुःखमोहात्मतया तथात्वमनुमेयं तद्वदेव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न [[चेन्द्रियाणामाहङ्कारिकत्वस्याभ्युपेतस्य|चेन्द्रियाणाम् आहङ्कारिकत्वस्याभ्युपेतस्य]], [[साध्यन्त्वाभिमतपारार्थ्यधर्मस्य|साध्यत्वाभिमत-पारार्थ्य-धर्मस्य]] [[चासंहतपरार्थत्वस्यान्यथात्वापादनादुभयविशेषविरुद्धत्वं|चासंहत-परार्थत्वस्यान्यथात्वापादनाद् उभय-विशेष-विरुद्धत्वं]] हेतोः; अहङ्कारान्वय-व्यतिरेकानुविधानेन " देवा वैकारिकाः स्मृताः " इत्य् आद्यागम-बलेन प्रकाश-लाघव-गुणान्वयेन च वैकारिकाभिधान-सात्त्विकाहङ्कार-भेद-योनित्वस्येन्द्रियाणां प्रमाण-सिद्धस्य अपवादानुपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P70]] (A possible objection is that) when the senses are admitted to be derived from ahamkara and when the meaning of what is accepted as the sadhya, namely, the quality of existing for the sake of another is the quality of existing for the sake of another which is itself not a collocation, the respective reasons for the above only prove the opposite, and hence, they are subject to the fallacy of *ubhaya-viseşaviruddha.*[^70_123] (The Sankhya replies) this objection cannot be raised. Since the presence or the absence of the senses is dependent respectively upon the presence or the absence of ahamkāra, since there is support of scriptural passage such as, "The senses are considered to proceed from ahamkara,"[^70_124] since there is contact of qualities, viz., brightness and lightness[^70_125] (with the senses), the fact that the senses have for their source that variety of ahamkāra wherein the sattva quality predominates and which is known as *vaikārika* is well supported by evidence; hence, it would be improper to deny this fact.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^70_123]: It is interesting to note that this identical argument has been cited as an example of ubhayaviseşaviruddha (1. e. Dharmadharmyubhaya visēşaviruddha), by Kumārila Bhatta in his Sloka-Varttika Anumanapariccheda. sl. 105-7. The six varieties of viruddha-Dharmasvarūpabādha, Dharmaviseṣabadha, Dharmisvarupabādha, Dharmivišeṣabādha, Dharmadharmyu- bhayaviše şabadha-have, in later times, been reduced to one, since all of them, in the last resort, only prove the opposite of what is intended to be proved.
[^70_124]: *Vişnu* Purāna, I. ii.41.
[^70_125]: *Sankhya*-*Karika*, verse 13. Sattvam laghu prakasakamistam
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न चेन्द्रियाणामाहङ्कारिकत्वस्याभ्युपेतस्य, साध्यन्त्वाभिमतपारार्थ्यधर्मस्य चासंहतपरार्थत्वस्यान्यथात्वापादनादुभयविशेषविरुद्धत्वं हेतोः; अहङ्कारान्वयव्यतिरेकानुविधानेन " देवा वैकारिकाः स्मृताः " इत्याद्यागमबलेन प्रकाशलाघवगुणान्वयेन च वैकारिकाभिधानसात्त्विकाहङ्कारभेदयोनित्वस्येन्द्रियाणां प्रमाणसिद्धस्यापवादानुपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

आत्मनस् तु सङ्घातत्वे तस्यापि सङ्घातान्तरार्थतयानवस्थापत्त्या निष्प्रमाणकानेककल्पनाप्रसङ्गात्, अप्रयोजकत्वाच् च सङ्घातत्वस्य शेषित्वे, [[दृष्टान्तदृष्टाशेषधर्मोपस्थापनेऽअनुमानप्रामाण्य|दृष्टान्त-दृष्टाशेष-धर्मोपस्थापने ऽनुमान-प्रामाण्य]]स्यैवासम्भवापत्तेः तद्-असङ्घातत्वस्य चाप्रचाल्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even so, the belief that the self is not a collocation is unshakable, for the reason that (1) if the soul were itself a collocation as it would have to exist for the sake of another collocation, there would result an unending series, and, as a consequence, many things for which evidence is lacking would have to be assumed; (2) the quality of being a collocation is not responsible for an entity being a śeşi (i. e. one for whose sake others exist); and (3) inference itself would lose its validity, if also the qualities found in the illustrative examples are taken into consideration.[^70_126]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^70_126]: Cf. yadi vivakṣitārthavyatirekeņa anumānasya avivakṣitamapi vişayaḥ, manvetasyām kalpaṇāyām sarvānumānam vyāhanyeta. Nyāya-Vārtika (Chowkamba edn. pp. 344-45). See also Nyayavārtikaṭālparyatīkā (Benares edn. p. 600).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

आत्मनस्तु सङ्घातत्वे तस्यापि सङ्घातान्तरार्थतयानवस्थापत्त्या निष्प्रमाणकानेककल्पनाप्रसङ्गात्, अप्रयोजकत्वाच्च सङ्घातत्वस्य शेषित्वे, दृष्टान्तदृष्टाशेषधर्मोपस्थापनेऽअनुमानप्रामाण्य स्यैवासम्भवापत्तेः तदसङ्घातत्वस्य चाप्रचाल्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च प्रमाणान्तर-बलेनानाहङ्कारिकत्वसङ्घातान्तरार्थत्वयोर् बाधे ऽबाधितेन सङ्घात-परार्थत्वेनापि न भवितव्यम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

When the refutation of the statements-that the senses do not proceed from ahamkāra ; and that the body, senses and the like exist for the sake of other collocations--is effected on the strength of some evidence, it will not necessarily follow that even the facts of their being a collocation and of their existing for the sake of others, which are uncontradicted, should stand condemned.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच प्रमाणान्तरबलेनानाहङ्कारिकत्वसङ्घातान्तरार्थत्वयोर्बाधेऽबाधितेन सङ्घातपरार्थत्वेनापि न भवितव्यम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एवं च संहतत्व-व्यापकावरुद्धत्रैगुण्यादिरहितो ऽसंहत आत्मा सिद्धः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P71]] Thus, it is evident that the soul, which is itself not a collocation, is free from the three guņas (sattva, rajas and tamas) which are associated with the quality of existing for the sake of another--a quality which never fails to be present whenever the character of being a collocation exists.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

एवं च संहतत्वव्यापकावरुद्धत्रैगुण्यादिरहितोऽसंहत आत्मा सिद्धः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा देहादयः सुख-दुःख-मोहात्मकतया परेणाधिष्ठीयन्ते, यन्त्रादिभिरिव रथादयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Being of the nature of pleasure, pain and misery, the body and the like are controlled by some other entity, even as the chariot and other objects by the charioteer and the like.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथा देहादयः सुखदुःखमोहात्मकतया परेणाधिष्ठीयन्ते, यन्त्रादिभिरिव रथादयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अपि चानुकूल-प्रतिकूल-वेदनीये [[सुखदुःखेभृत्यभ्रातृव्यवदनुकूलनीयप्रतिकूलनीयवती|सुख-दुःखे भृत्य-भ्रातृव्यवद् अनुकूलनीय-प्रतिकूलनीयवती]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Further, pleasure and pain, which are respectively known as agreeable and disagreeable experiences, point to a person who is pleased or displeased, even as the servant and the foe (imply a person who is ministered unto or one who is hated).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अपि चानुकूलप्रतिकूलवेदनीये सुखदुःखेभृत्यभ्रातृव्यवदनुकूलनीयप्रतिकूलनीयवती ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

दृश्यत्वाद् देहादयो घटादय इव [[विलक्षणद्रष्ट्टका|विलक्षण-द्रष्टृका]] इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Since the body, etc., are perceptible, like pots and similar objects, they must have a perceiver[^71_127] distinct from themselves.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^71_127]: In interpreting bhoktṛbhāvāt, some have understood bhoktā as enjoyer, and some, as perceiver. Both the interpretations have been mentioned here. See Sankhya*-*tattva-kaumudi, Kārikā, 17.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

दृश्यत्वाद्देहादयो घटादय इव विलक्षणद्रष्ट्टका इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अधिष्ठातुर अनुकूल-प्रतिकूल-वेदकस्य द्रष्टुः त्रैगुण्यादि-विपर्ययः पूर्ववदेव निर्णेतव्यः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

As shown before, the absence of the three gunas from the soul, who is (thus known to be) a controller, a knower of agreeable and disagreeable things and a perceiver, is definitely ascertainable.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अधिष्ठातुरनुकूलप्रतिकूलवेदकस्य द्रष्टुः त्रैगुण्यादिविपर्ययः पूर्ववदेव निर्णेतव्यः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा देहादेर् अव्यक्तान्तस्य [[कृत्स्न्स्य|कृत्स्नस्य]] त्रिगुणात्मकतयात्यन्त-दुःखोपशमन-लक्षण-मोक्ष-दशानुपपत्तेः तदर्थं च शास्त्राणां महाधियां च प्रवृत्तेरस्ति देहादि-व्यतिरिक्तो ऽसंहतः त्रैगुण्याद्यसंस्पृष्टः पुरुष इति ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Similarly, as all things commencing from the body and ending, with unmanifest matter (avyakta) are of the nature of the three guņas, the state of release, which is essentially the annihilation of all miseries, is impossible of attainment by them; but, since the śastras and wise men endeavour to attain (release), there must be a soul (purușa) that is distinct from the body, that is not a collocation, and that is untouched by the three guņas.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथा देहादेरव्यक्तान्तस्य कृत्स्न्स्य त्रिगुणात्मकतयात्यन्तदुःखोपशमनलक्षणमोक्षदशानुपपत्तेः तदर्थं च शास्त्राणां महाधियां च प्रवृत्तेरस्ति देहादिव्यतिरिक्तोऽसंहतः त्रैगुण्याद्यसंस्पृष्टः पुरुष इति ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति साङ्ख्याभिमतात्मानुमान-निरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति साङ्ख्याभिमतात्मानुमाननिरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति साङ्ख्याभिमतात्मानुमाननिरूपणम्)
</details>

#### खण्डनम्
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Refutation of the Sankhya Arguments
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अत्रापि सङ्घात-पारार्थ्यादिभिर् यद्यपि परः को ऽप्य् अधिष्ठाता द्रष्टा सिद्धः, तथापि न [[तस्यासंहतत्वात्रिगुणत्वादिरभिमतविशेषः|तस्य असंहतत्वात् त्रिगुणत्वादिर]] अभिमत-विशेषः शक्य-निश्चयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even here, although with the aid of reasons, such as that collocations exist for the sake of others, the existence of some other entity (than the body), who is a controller and perceiver is established, yet, (with their aid) the qualities of not being a collocation and of not possessing the three guņas, which are admitted by you, cannot be determined as belonging to it.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अत्रापि सङ्घातपारार्थ्यादिभिर्यद्यपि परः कोऽप्यधिष्ठाता द्रष्टा सिद्धः, तथापि न तस्यासंहतत्वात्रिगुणत्वादिरभिमतविशेषः शक्यनिश्चयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा हि — सङ्घातस्य सङ्घातान्तरार्थत्व-नियम-दर्शन-बलाद् आपतन्ती परापरा सङ्घात-कल्पना न दोषाय, कार्यतयेवानादि-कारण-परम्परा-परिकल्पना ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

To explain-The positing of a series of collocations, made on the strength of the observation that a collocation always exists only for another collocation, like the positing of a series of causes having no beginning, made for the reason that something is an effect, is not wrong.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाहिसङ्घातस्य सङ्घातान्तरार्थत्वनियमदर्शनबलादापतन्ती परापरा सङ्घातकल्पना न दोषाय, कार्यतयेवानादि कारणपरम्परापरिकल्पना ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च अप्रयोजकत्वम् अपि; असङ्घातस्य असङ्गस्य अशेष-विक्रिया-शून्यस्य अनाधेयातिशय-कूटस्थ-चिति-मात्र-वपुषः पुरुषस्य सङ्घातं प्रति परत्वानुपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P72]] It cannot be said that (the quality of being a collocation) is not responsible (for anything being a seși, an independent being for whose sake others exist); for, in respect of any collocation, the soul, which is not a collocation, which is unattached, which is bereft of all modifications and which is mere consciousness itself, which is unchanging and for which no service is rendered by anything else, cannot be that other for whose sake the collocation exists.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नचाप्रयोजकत्वमपि; असङ्घातस्यासङ्गस्याशेषविक्रियाशून्यस्यानाधेयातिशयकूटस्थचितिमात्रवपुषः पुरुषस्य सङ्घातं प्रति परत्वानुपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तद् हि तस्य शेषि भवति, तच् च तदर्थम्; यद् येनोपक्रियते क्रियते वा, यच् च उपकरोति करोति वा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That which is served or produced by another becomes the seși in respect of that other. That which serves or produces anything exists for the sake of the latter.[^72_128]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^72_128]: Cf. Jaimini-Sutra, III. i. 1 - sesih pararthatavat.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तद्वि तस्य शेषि भवति, तच्च तदर्थम्; यद्येनोपक्रियते क्रियते वा, यच्चोपकरोति करोति वा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च तथा साङ्ख्य-पुरुष इति कतं तस्य सङ्घातं प्रति परत्वं ? कथन्तरां च सङ्घातस्य तादर्थ्यं ? ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

But, since the puruşa admitted by the Sankhyas is not so (served or produced by a collocation), how can he be regarded as being that other in respect of the collocation? What is more, how can the collocation be treated as existing for his sake?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच तथा साङ्ख्यपुरुष इति कतं तस्य सङ्घातं प्रति परत्वं ? कथन्तरां च सङ्घातस्य तादर्थ्यं ? ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अनुपकार्यो ऽप्य् उपकार्यतया ऽऽत्मानं मन्यत इति चेत्; कामं मन्यताम्; किम् आयातम् उपकार्यत्वस्य? ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it be said that though the purusa is not really rendered any service, he imagines himself as being served, (we reply) by all means let him imagine like that; how does it help to establish that he is being served?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनुपकार्योप्युपकार्यतयाऽत्मानं मन्यत इति चेत्; कामं मन्यताम्; किमायातमुपकार्यत्वस्य? ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न खलु बालाः तल-मलिनतादि-मत्तया गगनम् अभिमन्यन्त इति तस्य तथात्वं भवति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

For the reason that children imagine ether to possess the dirt found in a region, the character of being dirty will not belong to it.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न खलु बालास्तलमलिनतादिमत्तया गगनमभिमन्यन्त इति तस्य तथात्वं भवति ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The impossibility of a conscious and changeless entity being the victim of illusions :-
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अपि च तथाविध-भ्रमो ऽपि कस्य कथम् उदयत इति विवेचनीयम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Further, to whom such an illusion occurs and how must be investigated.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अपि च तथाविधभ्रमोऽपि कस्य कथमुदयत इति विवेचनीयम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न तावच् चिति-शक्तेः; सर्व-विक्रिया-शून्यतयातिविशुद्धायाम् अशुभ-शत-निदान-भूत-भ्रम-परिणामासम्भवात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It cannot occur to the power of consciousness; for, the illusion, which is a mode of change and which is the root cause of a hundred ills, cannot arise in the exceedingly pure consciousness, as it is devoid of all modifications.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न तावच्चितिशक्तेः; सर्वविक्रियाशून्यतयातिविशुद्धायामशुभशतनिदानभूतभ्रमपरिणामासम्भवात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अन्तःकरणं तु बुद्ध्य्-अपर-परिभाषाभिधानम् अचेतनतया तनुर् इव न भ्राम्यति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P73]] The internal organ (antaḥkaraṇa) too, for which buddhi is another technical expression, cannot experience the illusion; for, like the body, it is non-intelligent.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अन्तःकरणं तु बुद्ध्यपरपरिभाषाभिधानमचेतनतया तनुरिव न भ्राम्यति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अचिद् अपि स्वच्छतया चिति-च्छायापन्नं चेतनायत इति चेत्; न; नीरूपायाः चितेर् बुद्धेश् च छाया-तद्-ग्रहणानुपपत्ते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it be urged that, though it is non-intelligent, the internal organ, being transparent, receives the reflection of consciousness and becomes a conscious subject, as it were, (we reply) not so; for, reflection and its reception cannot properly belong (respectively) to consciousness and buddhi, which are alike formless.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अचिदपि स्वच्छतया चितिच्छायापन्नं चेतनायत इति चेत्; न; नीरूपायाः चितेर्बुद्धेश्च छायातद्ग्रहणानुपपत्ते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

छायैव छायेति चेत्; कः खलु इवार्थः? ; चिति-सारूप्यम् इति चेत्; हन्तैवम् अशेष-विकार-रहित-चिति-सारूप्यतापत्ताव् अन्तःकरणम् अपि प्रत्यस्तमित-समस्त-वृत्तिकम् आपद्यत इति दुरुपपादतरो ऽयं भ्रम-सुख-दुःखादि-विकार-योगः प्रत्यात्म-सिद्धः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it be contended that 'to be a reflection' is to be like it, (we ask) what is meant by 'being like' (consciousness)? If the reply is that it consists in having a nature similar to that of consciousness, (we rejoin) if, indeed, that were so, when buddhi attains similarity with consciousness which is free from all modifications, it too becomes devoid of all modifications; and hence, it would be impossible to account for the contact of modifications, such as, illusion, pleasure and pain, which are met with in every soul.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

छायैव छायेति चेत्; कः खलु इवार्थ? ;चितिसरूपत्वमिति चेत्; हन्तैवमशेषविकाररहितचितिसरूपतापत्तावन्तःकरणमपि प्रत्यस्तमितसमस्तवृत्तिकमापद्यत इति दुरुपपादतरोऽयं भ्रमसुखदुःखादिविकारयोगः प्रत्यात्मसिद्धः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

चेतनत्वेन सारूप्यम् इति चेत्; न; चितिर् एव हि ते पुरुषः, न चेतयिता ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it be said that buddhi has a nature similar to that of consciousness only in so far as it possesses consciousness, (we reply) not so; for, on your view, the soul is, in fact, consciousness itself and not a conscious entity;
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

चेतनत्वेन सरूपत्वमिति चेत्; न; चितिरेव हि ते पुरुषः, न चेतयिता ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यथा ऽह तत्रभवान् पतञ्जलिः " यदा चितिर् एव पुरुषः किम् अत्र केन व्यपदिश्यते " इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

the venerable Patañjali, for instance, asks 'If consciousness alone is the soul, what is it that is referred to here, and by what?'
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यथाऽह तत्रभवान्पतञ्जलिः " यदा चितिरेव पुरुषः किमत्र केन व्यपदिश्यत " इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अजडायमानत्वम् इवार्थ इति चेत्; अजडत्वम् अपि न ज्ञातृत्वातिरिक्तं किञ्चिद् इत्य् उक्तम् एव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it be urged that 'being like' (consciousness) means 'being like not-non-intelligent', (we reply that) it has already been shown that not being not-intelligent is nothing more than the quality of being a knower[^73_129]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^73_129]: "Being like a reflection of consciousness, it becomes a conscious entity as it were" was the reply to the question "How can the antahkarana, which is non-intelligent, be a conscious entity and experience illusions?" "Being like a reflection of consciousness'' when explained, finally amounts to 'being like a conscious entity.' Thus, the answer reduces itself to a tautological proposition "Being like a conscious entity, it becomes a conscious entity, as it were.'
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अजडायमानत्वमिवार्थ इति चेत्; अजडत्वमपि न ज्ञातृत्वा  तिरिक्त किञ्चिदित्युक्तमेव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तेनैव तद्-विवरणम् इति च न किञ्चिद् एतत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

and hence, this (interpretation of 'being like') is pointless.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तेनैव तद्विवरणमिति च न किञ्चिदेतत् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अपि च चिति-सन्निधानाधीनां बुद्धि-सिद्धिम् अभिदधानः कथम् इव तद्-अजडिमानं प्रतिजानीयात्? न च चिति-स्वान्तयोः बिम्ब-प्रतिबिम्बाधाराभिमतयोर् अन्यतरस्मिन्न् अप्य् अविद्यमानस्य विषय-विशेषोपरक्त-ज्ञातृत्व-लक्षण-धर्म-भेदस्य प्रतिबिम्बे सम्भवः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P74]] Further, how (we ask) can he who maintains that the existence of buddhi is dependent upon the nearness of consciousness posit its being not-non-intelligent? And, when this particular quality, known as the character of being a knower-a quality associated with some object or other-does not exist in either consciousness or buddhi, which are considered to be the original and the basis of reflection, it cannot occur in the reflection.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अपि च चितिसन्निधानाधीनां बुद्धिसिद्धिमभिदधानः कथमिव तदजडिमानं प्रतिजानीयात्? नच चितिस्वान्तयोर्बिम्बप्रतिबिम्बाधाराभिमतयोर्अन्यतरस्मिन्नप्यविद्यमानस्य विषयविशेषोपरक्तज्ञातृत्वलक्षणधर्मभेदस्य प्रतिबिम्बे सम्भवः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

प्रत्युक्तश् च अयं प्रतिबिम्ब-वादः प्रच्छन्न-बाह्य-मत-प्रत्यादेशे ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

This reflection theory has already been refuted while discarding the view of the heretics in disguise.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

प्रत्युक्तश्चायं प्रतिबिम्बवादः प्रच्छन्नबाह्यमतप्रत्यादेशे ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The refutation of the argument that the vṛttis of the antaḥkarana are superposed on the purusa.
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यद् उच्यते — निर्विकाराया अपि पुंसे तत्-सन्निधि-महिमसमुत्थापित-प्रमाण-विपर्ययादि-विचित्र-वृत्ति-भेदं स्वान्तम् एव स्व-वृत्तिं विषय-विशेषांश् च उपदर्शयति, सामन्त-चक्रम् इव [[पराक्रमीयः|पराक्रमीय-]] प्रतिबल-विलोलनादि-वृत्तीः स्वामिने, ततः साक्षी भोक्ता च अपदिश्यते, राजेति विक्रमी विजयी चेति; तद् अनुपपन्नम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It may be said that, though the puruşa (self) is changeless, the antaḥkarana itself, which possesses wonderful and diverse activities, such as *pramāņa* and *viparyaya*[^74_130] produced by the power belonging to the nearness of the purusa, exhibits its activities and different objects to the puruşa; and thereby, he comes to be called witness (sākṣi), enjoyer (bhoktā); just as the gathering of generals possessing extremely great valour exhibits to the master its activities, such as entering the enemy's camp and causing consternation therein, and, as a consequence, he comes to be termed a monarch, a man of valour and a conqueror. But, this view is unsound.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^74_130]: Pramana, *viparyaya*, vikalpa, *nidrā* and smrti are the five vṛttis of the antahkarana. For an account of these see Yoga-Sutras I.5-11.
\*The word *parakramiyah* has been formed in accordance with Panini's sutra 'vinmatcrluk' (V. iii. 65). Compare the stems srajiyas, tvaciyas. Atisayena parakramavat parakramiyah (one possessing extremely great valour). All printed books and manuscripts read pratibalavilolanadivrtti; but pratibalavilolanadivrttim is obviously a better reading.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यदुच्यतेनिर्विकारायापि पुंसे तत्सन्निधिमहिमसमुत्थापितप्रमाणविपर्ययादिविचित्रवृत्तिभेदं स्वान्तमेव स्ववृत्तिं विषयविशेषांश्चोपदर्शयति, सामन्तचक्रमिव पराक्रमीयः प्रतिबलविलोलनादिवृत्तीः स्वामिने, ततः साक्षी भोक्ता चापदिश्यते, राजेति विक्रमी विजयी चेति; तदनुपपन्नम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

द्रष्ट्रे हि दर्शनीयं दृश्यते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

In fact, it is only for the sake of the seer that the visible object is found to exist;
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

द्रष्ट्रे हि दर्शनीयं दृश्यते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च दृशि-मात्रात्म-वादिनां साङ्ख्यानां तद्-उपजीविनां च प्रच्छन्नानां द्रष्टृत्वं वास्तवम् अस्ति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

and for the Sankhyas or for their followers, the heretics in disguise, who alike maintain that consciousness alone is the soul, the quality of being the seer is not real.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच दृशिमात्रात्मवादिनां साङ्ख्यानां तदुपजीविनां च प्रच्छन्नानां द्रष्टृत्वं वास्तवमस्ति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च काल्पनिकेन शेषित्व-सम्भवः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

And, the quality of being a seși (one for whose sake others exist) cannot be brought about by the fictitiously imagined quality of being the seer.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच काल्पनिकेन शेषित्वसम्भवः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

कल्पनापि न सम्भवतीत्य् उक्तम् एव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, it has already been said that even this fictitious imagination cannot arise.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

कल्पनापि न सम्भवतीत्युक्तमेव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

राजा तु सामान्यतो विशेषतो वा तेषु कर्मसु अमात्यान् नियुञ्जानः तत्-फलम् ऐश्वर्यादि च आध्रुवानः स्व-स्वामि-भाव-हेतु-क्रय-प्रतिग्रह-जननादि-व्यापार-योजी न निष्क्रियस्य अनाधेयातिशयस्य पुंसो निदर्शनम् इति यत्किञ्चिद् एतत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P75]] (As for the analogy), the king, who commands his generals, in a general or in a specific manner, in those activities, and who acquires the fruits resulting therefrom, such as, sovereignty, and who engages in activities such as purchasing, receiving and inheriting,[^75_131] which are responsible for the relation of being owner and property, is not an analogue to the soul, which is inactive, and which is rendered no service by anybody; hence this view is valueless.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^75_131]: Perhaps, in preference to birth (janana) mention may be made of conquest (jaya), since, in the case of ksatriyas, conquest is regarded as a special title to ownership, cf. svami rikthakravasamvibhāga parigrahādhigameṣu | brāhmaṇasya adhikam labdham | kşatriyasya vijitam | nirviṣṭam vaišyasūdrayoḥ. Gautama Dharma-Sutra, X. 38-41.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

राजा तु सामान्यतो विशेषतो वा तेषु कर्मस्वमात्यान्नियुञ्जानः तत्फलमैश्वर्यादि चाश्रुवानः स्वस्वामिभावहेतुक्रयप्रतिग्रहजननादि व्यापारयोगी न निष्क्रियस्यानाधेयातिशयस्य पुंसो निदर्शनमिति यत्किञ्चिदेतत् ।
</details>

#### शास्त्रैकप्रमाणता

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

स्थूलो ऽहं, गच्छाम्य् अहम् इत्यादि-प्रत्यक्ष-मृदित-विषयतया प्रसिद्धैवातीत-कालता व्यतोरेकानुमान-भेदानाम् इत्य् आनुमानिकीयम् अप्य् आत्म-सिद्धिम् अश्रद्दधानाः श्रौतीम् एव तां श्रोत्रियाः सङ्गिरन्ते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The different arguments seeking to prove that the soul is distinct from the body and the like are well-known to be stultified (*atitakālatā*),[^75_132] in as much as their subject-matter is shattered by perceptual knowledge, such as, 'I am stout,' 'I go,'; for this reason, those well-versed in the vedas, having no faith even in the view that the proof of the soul is afforded by inference, assert that this proof is furnished by the vedas alone.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^75_132]: The fallacy of atitakalata or kalatyayapadesa has, in later Nyaya terminology, come to be called *badha*.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

स्थूलोऽहं, गच्छाभ्यहमित्यादिप्रत्यक्षमृदितविषयतया प्रसिद्धैवातीतकालता व्यतोरेकानुमानभेदानामित्यानुमानिकीमप्यात्मसिद्धिमश्रद्दधानाः श्रौतीमेव तां श्रोतियाः सङ्गिरन्ते ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The existence of the soul established by sruti and srutyarthāpatti.
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

श्रुतयो हि साक्षाद् एव आत्मनः शरीरादि-व्यतिरेकम् आदर्शयन्ति ऽस एष नेति नेति ऽऽअकायमव्रणमस्नाविरं शुद्धमपापविद्धम् ऽऽयोनिमन्ये प्रपद्यन्ते शरीरत्वाय देहिनः । स्थाणुमन्ये ऽऽन जायते म्रियते वा कदाचित् ऽऽजीवापेतं वावकिलेदं म्रियते ऽऽन हि वै सशरीरस्य सतः प्रियाप्रिययोरपहतिरस्ति । अशरीरं वाव सन्तं न प्रियाप्रिये स्पृशतः ऽ इत्याद्याः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

In fact, scriptural passages, such as the following, directly reveal the distinctness of the soul from the body and the like." The soul (ātmā) is not this; it is not that." [^75_133]" The bodiless, the scatheless, the sinewless, the pure (śuddha), unpierced by sins (apāpaviddha) "; [^75_134] Some go into a womb for assuming bodily form; others become immovable objects"; [^75_135] "He is never born, nor does he die "; " Indeed, only this (body) which is devoid of life dies "[^75_136] "Verily, there is no freedom from pleasure and pain so long as he is embodied; when he is bodiless, pleasure and pain do not touch him." [^75_137]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^75_133]: *Brh*. *Up*.
[^75_134]: *Isa*. Up. 8.
[^75_135]: *Katha*. Up. V. 7.
[^75_136]: *Chand*. *Up.* VI. xi. 3.
[^75_137]: *Chand*. Up. VIII. xii. 1.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

श्रुतयो हि साक्षादेवात्मनः शरीरादिव्यतिरेकमादर्शयन्ति ऽस एष नेति नेतिऽऽअकायमव्रणमस्नाविरं शुद्धमपापविद्धम्ऽऽयोनिमन्ये प्रपद्यन्ते शरीरत्वाय देहिनः । स्थाणुमन्येऽऽन जायते म्रियते वा कदाचित्ऽऽजीवापेतं वावकिलेदं म्रियतेऽऽन हि वै सशरीरस्य सतः प्रियाप्रिययोरपहतिरस्ति । अशरीरं वाव सन्तं न प्रियाप्रिये स्पृशतःऽ इत्याद्याः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

कालान्तर-भावि-स्वर्गादि-साधन-विधयश् च आक्षिपन्ति देहादि-व्यतिरिक्तं नित्यं चेतनम् इति श्रुति-तद्-अनुपपत्ति-प्रमाणको ऽयं प्रत्यगात्मेति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P76]] Even the injunctions prescribing means for realising heavenly bliss and the like, which are to accrue after bodily death, lead to the positing of an eternal, conscious entity, that is distinct from the body, and so on; hence, the individual soul has for its means of proof the scripture and the presumptive testimony connected therewith (*śrutyarthāpatti*).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

कालान्तरभाविस्वर्गादिसाधनविधयश्चाऽक्षिपन्ति देहादिव्यतिरिक्तं नित्यं चेतनमिति श्रुतितदनुपपत्तिप्रमाणकोऽयं प्रत्यगात्मेति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मनः शास्त्रैक-प्रमाणकत्व-पक्ष-निरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मनः शास्त्रैकप्रमाणकत्वपक्षनिरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मनः शास्त्रैकप्रमाणकत्वपक्षनिरूपणम्)
</details>

### मीमांसक-प्रत्यक्षता
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

(c) The Mimamsā view :—

The existence of the jiva deduced from sense perception
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ननु हिताहित-प्राप्ति-परिहार-मात्र-परस्य आम्नायस्य शिरसि किम् इति महान् अयं भारः प्रक्षिप्यते?
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(One may ask) why should this heavy load be placed on the head of the vedas, whose sole aim is to teach the means for realising the good and avoiding the evil?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ननु हिताहितप्राप्तिपरिहारमात्रपरस्याऽम्नायस्य शिरसि किमिति महानयं भारः प्रक्षिप्यते?
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अनुमानागमाद्य्-अशेष-प्रमाण-मूल-भूतेन प्रत्यक्षेणैव ह्य् एनं प्रतिपद्यामहे ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Indeed, we know the soul with the aid of the testimony of perception itself, which is the basis of all pramāņas, such as, inference and scripture.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनुमानागमाद्यशेषप्रमाणमूलभूतेन प्रत्यक्षेणैव ह्येनं प्रतिपद्यामहे ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ममेदं शरीरम्, इदमहं जानामीति घटादिदृश्येभ्य इवायं द्रष्टा देहादपि पृथग्भूतः प्रत्यक्षं परिस्फुरति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

From cognitions such as, 'This is my body,' 'I know this,' it is evident that this seer shines forth in direct perception as being distinct from the body also, just as he is distinct from objects known, such as, the pot.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ममेदं शरीरम्, इदमहं जानामीति घटादिदृश्येभ्य इवायं द्रष्टा देहादपि पृथग्भूतः प्रत्यक्षं परिस्फुरति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इत्य् आत्मनः प्रत्यक्षत्व-पक्षोपक्षेपः)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इत्यात्मनः प्रत्यक्षत्वपक्षोपक्षेपः)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इत्यात्मनः प्रत्यक्षत्वपक्षोपक्षेपः)
</details>

#### प्रत्याक्षेपः
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Refutation of this view
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

मैवं वोचः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(We reply) do not say so; 
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

मैवं वोचः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

इन्द्रियार्थ-सन्निकर्ष-जं हि विज्ञानं प्रत्यक्षम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

for that is perceptual knowledge which arises from the contact of the senses with objects;[^76_138]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^76_138]: indriarthasannikarṣotpannam jñānam ..pratyakṣam. *Nyāya*-Sutras, I. i. *4*.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

इन्द्रियार्थसन्निकर्षजं हि विज्ञानं प्रत्यक्षम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च इन्द्रियाणि रूपादि-व्यतिरेकिणि निरतिशय-सूक्ष्मे प्रतीचि परागर्थ इव सन्निकर्षेण ज्ञानं जनयितुम् अर्हन्ति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

and from their contact with the inward soul, which is devoid of colour and other qualities, and which is exceedingly subtle, unlike their contact with outward objects, the senses are incapable of originating knowledge (concerning the soul).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नचेन्द्रियाणि रूपादिव्यतिरेकिणि निरतिशयसूक्ष्मे प्रतीचि परागर्थ इव सन्निकर्षेण ज्ञानं जनयितुम्अर्हन्ति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यथा आम्नायते ऽपराञ्चि खानि व्यतृणत् स्वयम्भूः ऽ इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It has been so declared in the vedas: "The self-existent (svayambhūḥ) made the senses proceed outward (and thus troubled them)."[^76_139]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^76_139]: Katha. Up. IV. I.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यथा आम्नायतेऽपराञ्चिरवानि व्यतृणत्स्वयम्भूःऽ इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

1.17 अचित्त्व-प्रतिबद्धश् च सर्वो ऽपीन्द्रिय-गोचरः ।  
तेन नैन्द्रियिकं ज्ञानम् आत्मानं स्प्रष्टुम् अर्हति ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

1.17 All objects revealed by the senses will invariably be accompanied by the quality of non-intelligence; therefore the knowledge born of the senses is incapable of touching the soul.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

1.17 अचित्त्वप्रतिबद्धश्च सर्वोऽपीन्द्रियगोचरः ।  
तेन नैन्द्रियिकं ज्ञानमात्मानं स्प्रष्टुमर्हति ॥
</details>

#### भाट्ट-मतम्
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The Bhaṭṭa view :-

The existence of the soul established through perception by manas

</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

स्यान् मतम् — भौतिकत्वात् बहिरिन्द्रियाणि मा नामात्मनि प्रवर्तिषत ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It may be said, "Let the external senses not come into contact with the soul and present it, since they are elemental (bhautika);
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

स्यान्मतम्भौतिकत्वाद्बहिरिन्द्रियाणि मा नामात्मनि प्रवर्तिषत ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

मनस् तु प्रवर्तिष्यते अभौतिकत्वाद् इति; तन् न; तस्यापीन्द्रियत्वे भौतिकत्वस्यापरिहार्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

but the manas, being non-elemental, may enter into contact with the soul and present it." (Against this, we reply) it is not so; for, if that too be a sense-organ, it must inevitably be elemental.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

मनस्तु प्रवर्तिष्यते अभौतिकत्वादिति; तन्न; तस्यापीन्द्रियत्वे भौतिकत्वस्यापरिहार्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यथा ऽऽम्नायते ऽअन्नमयं हि सोम्य मनः ऽ इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P77]] It has been so declared in the veda: "Gentle sir! the manas is, indeed, made of food (anna)";[^77_140]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^77_140]: *Chand*. Up. VI.v.4.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यथाऽम्नायतेऽअन्नमयं हि सोम्य मनःऽ इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

प्रपञ्चितं च एतत् निरूपणे ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

when dealing with manas it has been fully explained.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

प्रपञ्चितं चैतन्निरूपणे ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इत्य् आत्मनो ऽप्रत्यक्षत्व-शङ्का)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इत्यात्मनोऽप्रत्यक्षत्वशङ्का)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इत्यात्मनोऽप्रत्यक्षत्वशङ्का)
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अथोच्येत — अस्ति तावद् अहम् इत्य् अपरोक्षावभासः प्रत्ययः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It may be urged: "Certainly, there is a cognition of 'I' a cognition which is direct awareness.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अथोच्येतास्ति तावदहमित्यपरोक्षावभासः प्रत्ययः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च ऐन्द्रियिकत्वम् अन्तरेणासौ सम्भवति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

And this (cognition) cannot but be what has arisen from the senses.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न चैन्द्रियिकत्वमन्तरेणासौ सम्भवति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

कॢप्तं च बहिरिन्द्रियागोचरे ऽपि सुखादौ स्वान्त-स्वातन्त्र्यम् इति तन्-निमित्त एवायम् अहम्-प्रत्ययो युक्तः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The claim of manas in regard to (the manifestation of) pleasure and the like, even though they do not fall within the scope of the external senses, is well established. Hence, it is but proper that the cognition of 'I' should have this for its cause.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

क्ल्प्तं च बहिरिन्द्रियागोचरेऽपि सुखादौ स्वान्तस्वातन्त्र्यमिति तन्निमित्त एवायमहम्प्रत्ययो युक्तः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

प्रयोगश् च भवति — आत्मा मानस-प्रत्यक्ष-ग्राह्यः बहिरिन्द्रियायोग्यत्वे सति प्रत्यक्षत्वात् सुखादि-वद् इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

This can be expressed syllogistically. The soul, like pleasure and so on, is to be grasped by mental perception; for, while it is not capable of being grasped by the external senses, it is still an object of perception."
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

प्रयोगश्च भवतिआत्मा मानसप्रत्यक्षग्राह्यः बहिरिन्द्रियायोग्यत्वे सति प्रत्यक्षत्वात्सुखादिवतिति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति भाट्ट-मुखेनात्मनो मानस-प्रत्यक्षत्वानुमानोपक्षेपः)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति भाट्टमुखेनात्मनो मानसप्रत्यक्षत्वानुमानोपक्षेपः)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति भाट्टमुखेनात्मनो मानसप्रत्यक्षत्वानुमानोपक्षेपः)
</details>

##### प्रत्याक्षेपः
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Refutation of this view
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तन् न; संवेदनेन व्यभिचारात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(Our reply is) it is not so; for, from the case of (samvedana) jñāna, (where the sadhya is absent while the hetu is present), it is found that this argument commits the fallacy of *vyabhicāra*.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तन्न; संवेदनेन व्यभिचारात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च तद् अप्रत्यक्षम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(To escape this fallacy), you cannot point out that jñāna is not open to perception;
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच तदप्रत्यक्षम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

जानामीत्य् अनन्योपाधिकतया प्रतिभानात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

for without depending on anything else, it manifests itself as 'I know';
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

जानामीत्यनन्योपाधिकतया प्रतिभानात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अप्रत्यक्षत्वे च संवेदनस्य असिद्धिर् एव स्याद् इत्य् उक्तम् एव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

and it has already been stated that if it were not an object of perception, it would, in fact, cease to be knowledge.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अप्रत्यक्षत्वे च संवेदनस्यासिद्धिरेव स्यादित्युक्तमेव ।
</details>

#### न मानस-प्रत्यक्षम्
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Untenability of the suggestion that jnāna is the object of mental perception:-
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च तद् अपि मानस-प्रत्यक्षतया सपक्षे निक्षेपम् अर्हति; विमर्दासहत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It cannot be contended that, since it is an object of mental perception, jñāna too is fit to rank among similar examples (sapaksa); for this contention will not stand scrutiny.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच तदपि मानसप्रत्यक्षतया सपक्षे निक्षेपमर्हति; विमर्दासहत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यदा खलु कुतश्चिद् आत्म-मनः-संयोगाद् विषय-संवित्-उदयम् आसादयति, तदैव किं तत एव तद्-गोचरम् अपि वेदनं जन्यते, उतानिदान्येनेति वाच्यम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(If that is your view), you must point out whether even the knowledge concerning the knowledge of an object is produced exactly at the time when, by virtue of a certain conjunction between soul and manas, the knowledge of an object takes birth, and whether (it is produced) by the selfsame contact, or whether it is produced at a different time and by a different contact.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यदा खलु कुतश्चिदात्ममनःसंयोगाद्विषयसंवितुदयमासादयति, तदैव किं तत एव तद्गोचरमपि वेदनं जन्यते, उतान्यदान्येनेति वाच्यम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च युगपद् उभय-जननं सम्भाव्यते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(Regarding the first alternative), the origination of the two (i. e. knowledge of an object and knowledge concerning the knowledge of that object) at the same time is impossible.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच युगपदुभयजननं सम्भाव्यते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा हि सति परापर-तत्तद्-गोचर-निरवधिक-धी-निकुरुम्ब-जन्म तत्कालम् एवापद्येत ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If that were so, the birth of a collection of limitless items of knowledge, each of which has the other for its respective object, would have to take place at the same time.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाहिसति परापरतत्तद्गोचरनिरवधिकधीनिकुरुम्बजन्म तत्कालमेवापद्येत ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च तद् अस्ति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

But it does not take place.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच तदस्ति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

युगपद्-उत्पत्तौ विषय-विषयित्व-नियमश् च निर्निबन्धनः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it takes place simultaneously, the distinction made between being an object of knowledge and owning the object (visayaviṣayitvaniyamah) would become baseless.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

युगपदुत्पत्तौ विषयविषयित्वनियमश्च निर्निबन्धनः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

असमसमय-जन्मना ज्ञानेन वेद्यत्वे न प्रत्यक्षत्वम्; क्षणिकत्वेनाग्रिम-ज्ञानस्य आग्राहक-ज्ञानोदयम् अवस्थानाभावात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(Regarding the second alternative), if it (knowledge concerning knowledge) is made known by a knowledge arising at a different time, it would cease to be an object of perception; for, as knowledge is momentary, the earlier knowledge will not last till the rise of the knowledge which reveals it.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

असमसमयजन्मना ज्ञानेन वेद्यत्वे न प्रत्यक्षत्वं; क्षणिकत्वेनाग्रिमज्ञानस्य आग्राहकज्ञानोदयमवस्थानाभावात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

भावे च सर्व-ज्ञानानां सर्वदावस्थान-प्रसङ्गात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it lasts, all cognitions would have to exist at all times.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

भावे च सर्वज्ञानानां सर्वदावस्थानप्रसङ्गात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

कार्य-विरोधित्वे च अनन्तरम् एव संस्कारोदयान् न कालान्तरे स्थितिरिति संविदो न मानस-प्रत्यक्ष-वेद्यत्वम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it be urged that it is incompatible with its effect (i.e. if it perishes as soon as its effect springs up), (we reply that) as its effect namely the mental impression arises immediately after, it will not exist at a different time (i. e. at a time when the revealing consciousness arises). Hence jnana cannot be an object of mental perception.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

कार्यविरोधित्वे चानन्तरमेव संस्कारोदयान्न कालान्तरे स्थितिरिति संविदो न मानसप्रत्यक्षवेद्यत्वम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च अप्रत्यक्षा संविद् इति स्फुटो व्यभिचारः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

And it cannot be said that it is obvious that the argument commits the fallacy of vyabhicāra.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नचाप्रत्यक्षा संविदिति स्फुटो व्यभिचारः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ऐन्द्रियिकत्वस्य अनात्मत्व-प्रतिबद्धत्वाद् विरुद्धता च ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, as the quality of being grasped by the senses is invariably concomitant with the quality of being non-soul, your argument commits the fallacy of *viruddha* also (i.e. is guilty of employing adverse probans).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ऐन्द्रियिकत्वस्यानात्मत्वप्रतिबद्धत्वाद्विरुद्धता च ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

साध्य-विकलश् च दृष्टान्तः, सुख-दुःखयोः प्रत्यक्षत्वानभ्युपगमात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P78]] Further the illustrative example cited in the argument is defective in not possessing the sadhya; for, pleasure and pain are not admitted to be objects of perception.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

साध्यविकलश्च दृष्टान्तः, सुखदुःखयोः प्रत्यक्षत्वानभ्युपगमात् ।
</details>

#### सुख-दुःखे
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Enquiry into the nature of sukha, duhkha etc:-
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अनभ्युपगमश् च इन्द्रिय-पौष्कल्य-नाशयोर् एव सुख-दुःखत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

And it is not so admitted, because pleasure and pain are nothing more than the flourishing or the decaying state of the senses.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनभ्युपगमश्चेन्द्रियपौष्कल्यनाशयोरेव सुखदुःखत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न हि तस्मिन्न् अप्रत्यक्षे तत्-पौष्कल्यं वैकल्यं वा प्रत्यक्षं भवति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Indeed, when the senses are not perceptible, their flourishing or decaying state will not be the object of perception.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नहि तस्मिन्नप्रत्यक्षे तत्पौष्कल्यंवैकल्यं वा प्रत्यक्षं भवति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

इन्द्रिय-स्वरूप इव अभ्यास-पाटवात् तयोर् अपरोक्षत्वाभिमानः, मनोZवस्था-भेदेष्व् इव चानुमेय-मनो-वादिनाम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

In the case of pleasure and pain, as in that of the senses, or again, in that of the different states of mind (manas) on the view of those who maintain that manas is inferable, the false impression that they are directly perceived is due to the power of long continued experience.[^78_141]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^78_141]: With continued practice one infers the existence of pleasure, pain, the states of mind and the like so effortlessly and quickly and without noticing the several steps of the argument, that one comes to think that he directly perceives them.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

इन्द्रियस्वरूप इवाभ्यासपाटवात्तयोरपरोक्षत्वाभिमानः, मनोऽवस्थाभेदेष्विव चानुमेयमनोवादिनाम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यस् तु सुगत-मतावलम्बी विज्ञानाभिन्न-हेतु-जत्या तयोर् अपि तद्-अन्तर्भावम् अभिमन्यते; कण-भक्ष-पक्षाश्रयणेन वा तयोर् आत्म-विशेष-गुणत्वम्; ताभ्यां सुख-दुःखाधिकरणं व्याचक्षीत; स्वतः सुखीत्य् एतद्-विमर्शो वा अत्रत्यः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P79]] The section dealing with pleasure and pain (sukhaduhkhādhi- *karaṇa*)[^79_142] or the discussion of the description of the soul as being in its essential nature blissful (svatassukhi) found in this work itself[^79_143] ought to be explained to those who, following the Buddhistic doctrine, believe that pleasure and pain are included in the category of knowledge, for the reason that they are produced by causes which are non-different from knowledge, and to those who, by accepting the system of Kanabhakṣa (the exponent of the Vaiseṣika system) believe that they are the special qualities of the soul (and not the flourishing and the decaying states of the senses).[^79_144]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^79_142]: Sukhaduḥkhādhikaraṇa is the sixth section of the first pāda of Nathamuni's *Nyāyataṭtva*-sastra, a work which is not extant now. Yamuna refers to a few other adhikaraṇas of this sastra. In fact, his *Atmasiddhi* may be regarded as a brief exposition of *Nyayatattva*. Compare *Nyāyasiddhāňjana*, Buddhipariccheda "Nyayatattva-prakaraṇam hi Atmasiddih"
[^79_143]: This discussion over svatassukhi is included among the portions of *Atmasiddhi* lost.
[^79_144]: Those who identify pleasure and pain with the flourishing or the decaying states of the senses mean by senses the internal sense (manas) and not the outer senses; for, pleasure and pain are nothing more than the tranquil and the disturbed states of manas. cf. tatha ca antahkaranaprasādā vasayda yoreva sukhatvaduhkhatvavyapadesadarsanat tatprasāda vasādā veva sukhaduhkarupā vityarthah. rāmānuja tika on *Nyāyasiddhānjana*, *Buddhipariccheda*. Ranga-. Though this view is defended here and elsewhere in *Atmasiddhi*, it cannot be considered to be his final view, for, later on, he says that all reference to certainty, doubt, pleasure, pain and the like has for its object either same particular form of contact of knowledge with its object or knowledge possessing that contact. cf. *Nyāyasiddhānjana*, *Buddhipariccheda* sukhaduhkheca natmadharmau ityāditu vaibhavena matantareņa vā abhihitam anyathā kathamevam upasamhārārambhe brüyāt ⚫tadevam atmasvabbāvabhūtasya caitanyasya visayasamŝleşavidaeşagocara eva niscayasamsayadi vyavahārabhedah tadviseṣabhāji caitanyevā. Rāmānuja says, in *Vedarthasamgraha*, that knowledge, which is in contact with a particular object, and which is considered the cause of pleasure or pain, is really pleasure or pain itself and not its cause. Besides knowledge, nothing else which could be called pleasure or pain is noticed.. yena vişayaviseşeņa viseşitam jñānam sukhasya janakamity abhimatam tadviṣayajñānameva sukham tadatireki padarthäntaram nopalabhyate "
\*The reading tatcalanam found in the Chowkamba and Telugu editions is manifestly wrong; it has been altered into cetaścalanam. If, however, the original reading must stand, the sentence "bhūtaduḥkhajñāne na taccalanam sokaḥ" must come after and not precede the sentence "agamitajjñā nena cetașcalanam bhayam."
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यस्तु सुगतमतावलम्बी विज्ञानाभिन्नहेतुजतया तयोरपि तदन्तर्भावमभिमन्यते; कणभक्षपक्षाश्रयणेन वा तयोरात्मविशेषगुणत्वम्;ताभ्यां सुखदुःखाधिकरणं व्याचक्षीत; स्वतःसुखीत्येतद्विमर्शं वात्रत्यम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

राग-द्वेषादयस् तु चैतन्यस्यैवावस्था-विशेषास् तद्वद् एव प्रत्यक्षीभवन्तीति न तन्-निदर्शनेनानुमानोदयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Being, in fact, only different states of consciousness, desire, aversion and the like must be perceptible, even as consciousness is; hence, with these as illustrative examples, you cannot advance your argument.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

रागद्वेषादयस्तु चैतन्यस्यैवावस्थाविशेषास्तद्वदेव प्रत्यक्षीभवन्तीति न तन्निदर्शनेनानुमानोदयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

सुख-प्रयुक्त-विषयीकार-चैतन्यं रागः, तद्-विरोध-प्रयुक्त-विषयीकारं तद् एव द्वेषः, भूत-दुःख-ज्ञानेन चेतश्-चलनं शोकः, आगामि-तज्-ज्ञानेन चेतश्-चलनं भयम् इत्यादि लक्षण-ग्रन्थाद् एवावगन्तव्यम् इत्य् अलं प्रविस्तरेण ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P80]] Desire is consciousness which is directed towards objects with a view to obtaining pleasure. The same (consciousness,) when directed towards objects, with a view to obtaining the opposite of pleasure, is aversion. Sorrow is mental agitation caused by consciousness of past pains. Fear is mental excitement produced by the awareness of pains to come. Since those (i.e., terms namely, desire, aversion, sorrow and fear) and others like them may be understood even from treatises dealing with definitions, it is needless to discuss them (here) at length.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

सुखप्रयुक्तविषयीकारचैतन्यं रागः, तद्विरोधप्रयुक्तविषयीकारं तदेव द्वेषः, भूतदुःखज्ञानेन चेतश्चलनं शोकः, आगामितज्ज्ञानेन चेतश्चलनं भयमित्यादि लक्षणग्रन्थादेवावगन्तव्यमित्यलं प्रविस्तरेण ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति गुरु-मुखेन आत्मनो मानस-प्रत्यक्षत्वानुमान-दूषणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति गुरुमुखेनात्मनो मानसप्रत्यक्षत्वानुमानदूषणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति गुरुमुखेनात्मनो मानसप्रत्यक्षत्वानुमानदूषणम्)
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एकस्य च आत्मनो निरंशस्य न स्वापेक्षया ग्राह्य-ग्राहक-भावः, विरोधाद् इत्य् अप्य् उक्तम् एव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It has already been shown that, as it involves a contradiction, one and the same self which is partless, cannot possess, in respect of itself, the quality of being at once the perceiver and the perceived.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

एकस्य चात्मनो निरंशस्य न स्वापेक्षया ग्राह्यग्राहकभावः, विरोधादित्यप्युक्तमेव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अंश-भेदाश्रयणे तत्-सिद्धये च अंशान्तरम् आश्रयितव्यम्, तथा तत्र तत्रेत्य् अनवस्था; सङ्घातत्वं च आत्मनः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If the distinction of parts (within the self) be admitted, to establish the same, (for each of these parts) other parts would have to be admitted; similarly, for these latter, other parts, and so on ad infinitum. Besides, the quality of being a collocation would have to be attributed to the soul.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अंशभेदाश्रयणे तत्सिद्धये चांशान्तरमाश्रयितव्यम्, तथा तत्र तत्रेत्यनवस्था; सङ्घातत्वं चात्मनः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति च आत्मनो ग्राह्य-ग्राहक-भावे विरोधोद्भावनम्)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति चात्मनो ग्राह्यग्राहकभावे विरोधोद्भावनम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति च आत्मनो ग्राह्यग्राहकभावे विरोधोद्भावनम्)
</details>

#### भाट्ट-मतम्
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The Bhatta view again:-
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ननु च ग्राहकावभासः श्रुत्या, स्व-सिद्धान्त-श्रद्धा-विप्रलब्ध-बुद्धिभिर् अभिहितः; इन्द्रियादि-प्रत्यासन्न-तत्तत्-पदार्थ-मात्र-स्फुरणात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(Here is yet another attempt to show that the self is open to mental perception). A consciousness, like the following: 'I perceive the pot' posited to exist on the strength of scriptural references to the awareness of the perceiver,[^80_145] by those whose intellect has been blinded by excessive faith in their own system, must be said to exist on some occasions (at least); for (often) only the several objects which are near the senses are apprehended (and not the self).
